---

# Prompt Refinery — Technical Overview

## 1. Purpose & Functionality

**Prompt Refinery** is a developer tool that transforms rough, vague AI prompts into well-
  structured, high-quality ones. It solves the friction of writing effective LLM prompts by
  automating the "prompt engineering" process through Claude.

Core user workflows:
- **Refine**: Paste a rough prompt → receive a structured rewrite with an explanation of changes and
  a quality scorecard
- **Follow-up**: Iteratively adjust the refined prompt via free-text feedback or quick presets
  (shorter, more formal, etc.)
- **Compare**: Run the same rough prompt through up to 4 Claude models simultaneously to compare
  results
- **A/B Test**: Run both the rough and refined prompts through Claude and see the output difference
  side-by-side
- **Run Prompt**: Launch a full multi-turn conversation with the refined prompt as the opener
- **Persist & Export**: History/saved prompts in `localStorage`; export to Markdown, JSON, or CSV;
  PDF export of entire sessions

---

## 2. Architecture & Structure

The codebase is split into three largely independent sub-applications sharing one backend:

```
prompt-improver/
├── server/          # Node.js / Express API server
│   └── index.js     # All backend logic in a single file
├── client/          # React SPA (Vite)
│   └── src/
│       ├── App.jsx            # Entire frontend application
│       ├── RunDrawer.jsx      # Slide-out conversation panel
│       ├── lint.js            # Client-side prompt linter
│       ├── scan.js            # Client-side PII scanner
│       ├── io.js              # Export/import logic
│       ├── icons.jsx          # SVG icon components
│       ├── help-content.js    # Static help text data
│       └── templates-content.js # Prompt templates data
└── extension/       # Chrome/Chromium Manifest V3 extension
    ├── popup.html / popup.js  # Self-contained popup UI
    └── config.js              # Configurable API URL
```

**Layer separation is intentional but lightweight** — there is no abstraction between layers within
  each sub-app (e.g., no store layer in the React app). The entire React frontend is a single `App`
  component tree with ~3900 lines.

---

## 3. Tech Stack

| Layer | Technology |
|---|---|
| **Client framework** | React 19 + Vite 8 |
| **CSS** | Plain CSS (`App.css`, `index.css`) — no CSS framework |
| **PDF generation** | jsPDF 4 + html2canvas (for rasterizing the radar chart) |
| **Markdown rendering** | react-markdown 10 + remark-gfm + react-syntax-highlighter |
| **Backend** | Node.js + Express 5 (ESM) |
| **AI API** | Anthropic SDK `@anthropic-ai/sdk` ^0.95 |
| **Streaming protocol** | Server-Sent Events (SSE), custom event names |
| **Auth / secrets** | `.env` file via `dotenv` |
| **Browser extension** | Vanilla JS, Chrome Manifest V3 |
| **Storage** | Browser `localStorage` only (no database) |
| **Dev tooling** | Vite, ESLint, nodemon |

---

## 4. Core Components

### `server/index.js` — The Backend (~420 lines)
A single-file Express server with four API routes. All routes stream responses over SSE using a pair
  of helper functions (`setupSSE`, `sendEvent`). Key internals:

- **`REFINER_SYSTEM_PROMPT`**: The heart of the product. Instructs Claude to act as a prompt-
  engineering specialist and return a structured response using custom delimiters
  (`<<<REFINED_PROMPT>>>`, `<<<CHANGES_JSON>>>`, `<<<SCORES_JSON>>>`, `<<<END>>>`).
- **`parseRefinerResponse()`**: Regex-based parser that extracts the three sections from Claude's
  raw text.
- **Streaming partial text**: On the `/api/improve` route, the server forward-streams only the
  `REFINED_PROMPT` section in real time as `refined-chunk` events, then emits `changes` and `scores`
  as complete JSON events after the stream finishes. This gives the user a visible typing effect for
  the result while the heavyweight JSON sections load invisibly.

### `client/src/App.jsx` — The Frontend (~3900 lines)
A monolithic React component with all UI and state management inlined. Notable sub-components:

| Component | Role |
|---|---|
| `App` | Root; owns all state via `useState`; orchestrates all async operations |
| `LintHintsPanel` | Renders heuristic lint hints below the composer |
| `PIIWarningModal` | Pre-send PII detection warning with edit/continue decision |
| `PDFPreviewModal` | Generates and previews a PDF via jsPDF; section-toggle UI |
| `RadarChart` | Pure SVG radar/spider chart for quality scores |
| `ScoresPanel` | Renders per-dimension scores with before/after comparisons |
| `ChangesPanel` | Numbered list of what the refiner changed |
| `ComparisonStrip` | Side-by-side grid of model comparison results |
| `ABTestPanel` | Two-column A/B test result view |
| `FollowUpPanel` | Preset buttons + free-text input for refinement feedback |
| `UsageView` | Cost/token dashboard with 7-day bar chart and per-model breakdown |
| `HistoryView`, `SavedView`, `TemplatesView`, `HelpView`, `SettingsView` | Left-rail drawer panels
  |

### `client/src/RunDrawer.jsx` — Conversation Panel
A slide-out `<aside>` dialog for multi-turn prompt execution. Renders assistant messages with full
  Markdown (GFM + syntax-highlighted code blocks via `react-syntax-highlighter`). Has two modes:
  `conversation` view and `list` view (previous conversations).

### `client/src/lint.js` — Prompt Linter
Eight pure heuristic checks run locally, zero API calls, triggered 400ms after the user stops
  typing. Checks include: too short, no concrete nouns, hedge words, missing
  audience/format/length/constraints/examples. Returns hints sorted by severity (`critical` →
  `warning` → `info`).

### `client/src/scan.js` — PII Scanner
Regex-based scanner with genuine false-positive mitigation:
- **Credentials**: OpenAI/Anthropic keys, GitHub PATs, Slack tokens, AWS access key IDs, generic
  `key=value` secrets
- **Financial**: Credit cards (Luhn check applied), US SSNs (range-validated), IBANs
- **Contact**: Emails, US/international phone numbers, street addresses

### `client/src/io.js` — Export/Import
Tri-format (JSON/Markdown/CSV) export with a built-in RFC-4180 CSV parser for import. JSON is the
  only lossless format; the Markdown importer recovers rough + refined text by parsing heading and
  code-fence structure. Duplicate detection on import uses `rough + improved + model` as a composite
  key.

### `extension/popup.js` — Browser Extension
~270 lines of vanilla JS. Connects to the same `/api/improve` SSE endpoint but buffers the entire
  stream before rendering (no progressive display). Reads the API URL from
  `window.PROMPT_REFINERY_CONFIG` to allow pointing at non-localhost deployments.

---

## 5. Data Flow

### Refinement flow (core path):
```
[User types rough prompt]
        │
        ▼
[lint.js] runs heuristics in browser (debounced 400ms)
        │
[scan.js] runs PII checks if enabled
        │ (if findings → PIIWarningModal → user decides to continue/cancel)
        ▼
POST /api/improve  { prompt, category, model, previousRefined?, feedback? }
        │
        ▼ (Express → Anthropic SDK streaming)
SSE: refined-chunk (one or many, builds up the displayed text)
SSE: refined-done
SSE: changes       { changes: [{title, explanation}, …] }
SSE: scores        { scores: { rough: {…}, refined: {…} } }
SSE: done          { usage: {inputTokens, outputTokens}, latencyMs }
        │
        ▼
[App.jsx] accumulates text → saves to localStorage history → records usage
```

### Comparison flow:
```
POST /api/improve-compare { prompt, category, models: [id1, id2, …] }
        │
        ▼ (Promise.allSettled — all models in parallel)
For each model → SSE: model-chunk, model-changes, model-scores, model-done
        │
        ▼
[App.jsx] updates each column independently → ComparisonStrip re-renders
```

### A/B test flow:
```
POST /api/test-prompt { prompts: [{id, prompt}], model }
        │
        ▼ (Promise.allSettled — rough + refined in parallel)
SSE: test-chunk (id, text), test-done (id, usage, latencyMs)
        │
        ▼
[App.jsx] updates rough/refined result columns independently
```

### Run-prompt (conversation) flow:
```
[User clicks "Run" or sends message]
        │
        ▼
POST /api/run-prompt { messages: [{role, content}, …], model }
        │
        ▼
SSE: run-chunk (text), run-done (usage, latencyMs)
        │
        ▼
[RunDrawer] appends to conversation → auto-archives to localStorage
```

---

## 6. Entry Points

| Entry | Description |
|---|---|
| `server/index.js` | `node index.js` or `npm run dev` (port 3001) |
| `client/src/main.jsx` | Vite SPA entry; mounts `<App />` into `#root` |
| `extension/popup.html` | Chrome extension popup, loads `popup.js` inline |
| `GET /api/health` | Healthcheck endpoint |

The API URL is configurable on the client via `VITE_API_URL` environment variable (defaults to
  `http://localhost:3001`).

## 8. Notable Patterns & Design Decisions

### SSE over WebSockets
All streaming uses Server-Sent Events with a custom event naming scheme (`refined-chunk`, `model-
  chunk`, etc.). The `consumeSSE` helper in `App.jsx` is a generic SSE reader that dispatches to a
  handler map by event name — essentially a mini event bus over HTTP.

### Structured response parsing via delimiters
Claude is instructed to output responses using `<<<DELIMITER>>>` markers. This is a deliberate
  alternative to asking for JSON output of the whole response, which would prevent streaming the
  refined text progressively. The server streams `REFINED_PROMPT` in real time and defers the JSON
  sections until the full response is available.

### Single-file monolith per layer
Both `server/index.js` and `client/src/App.jsx` are intentionally monolithic. The server is ~420
  lines; the client is ~3900 lines. This is a practical tradeoff for a solo/small-team project — no
  module indirection to navigate, but it would benefit from decomposition as the feature set grows.

### All persistence is client-side localStorage
No database, no user accounts. Everything (history, saved prompts, settings, usage records,
  conversations) lives in `localStorage`. Caps are enforced in code (`MAX_HISTORY = 20`,
  `MAX_CONVERSATIONS = 50`, `MAX_USAGE_RECORDS = 500`).

### AbortController chains
Every async operation (`refinement`, `comparison`, `abTest`, `run`) has its own `AbortController`
  stored in a `ref`. The "Stop" button calls `.abort()` on the active controllers. There is an
  acknowledged limitation in a code comment: the `/api/run-prompt` endpoint can't reliably detect
  client disconnect (due to a spurious `close` event during SSE header flushing in Node 20), so the
  Anthropic call finishes in the background even if the user closes the drawer.

### Browser-only privacy features
Both the linter and PII scanner run entirely in the browser with no server round-trip. This is
  explicitly highlighted in the UI ("runs in your browser — nothing has been sent yet") as a trust
  signal. The PII scanner uses Luhn validation for credit cards and area/group/serial validation for
  SSNs to reduce false positives.

### PDF generation is fully client-side
`jsPDF` constructs the PDF programmatically using coordinates. `html2canvas` is used only to
  rasterize the SVG radar chart (which jsPDF can't embed directly as SVG). The PDF modal debounces
  re-generation on section-toggle changes by 250ms to avoid thrashing.

### ⚠️ Flagged ambiguities
- The `server/package.json` has a duplicate `"keywords": []` key (cosmetic, harmless).
- Strange files at the repo root (`span`, `spanfirst-child`, `spanfirst-of-type`) appear to be
  filesystem artifacts from a macOS CSS copy-paste (the filenames look like CSS pseudo-selectors).
  These are untracked junk and can be deleted.
- The extension's `config.js` file is referenced in `popup.js` as `window.PROMPT_REFINERY_CONFIG`
  but is not listed in the extension's `manifest.json` content scripts. It would need to be loaded
  as a script in `popup.html` for the configurable URL to work.
- Model pricing in `PRICING` and the disclaimer in `UsageView` say "May 2026" — those rates and
  dates will need updating over time.

## The Reality

There's **no automatic sync** between Claude Code and Claude.ai — they're separate surfaces. But you
  can create a **single source-of-truth document** that both can use, which gets you 90% of the way
  there.

---

## Recommended Path: Two-Step Setup

### Step 1 — Create `CLAUDE.md` (for Claude Code)
This file lives in your project root and **Claude Code reads it automatically at the start of every
  session** — no manual pasting needed. It should contain architecture notes, dev commands, key
  patterns, and anything non-obvious.

### Step 2 — Upload that same file to a Claude.ai Project
In your Claude.ai Project:
1. Go to **Project → Add content** (or "Instructions")
2. Upload `CLAUDE.md`, or paste its contents into **Project Instructions** (the system prompt field)
3. Now every conversation in that Project starts with full codebase context

That's it. When the codebase changes, update `CLAUDE.md` in one place and re-upload.

  can verify it in the running app.

| What you want to add | Where it goes |

  `*View` component |
| New icon | `icons.jsx` |

| New help section | `help-content.js` |

3. **Junk files at repo root** — `span`, `span:first-child`, etc. to clean up
4. **`App.jsx` monolith** — extract `ComparisonStrip`, `ABTestPanel`, `PDFPreviewModal`, etc.
5. **Pricing data hardcoded** — May 2026 rates need a maintenance story

**Common feature ideas I might have suggested for a tool like this:**
- 🧵 Prompt chaining / template variables (`{{variable}}` substitution)
- 📊 History analytics (score trends over time, most-used categories)
- 🔁 "Re-refine" from history with a different model
- 🧩 Prompt snippets / reusable building blocks library
- 🌐 Share a refined prompt via a short link
- 🎨 Custom scoring dimensions

---

## 🎓 Git & GitHub — The Mental Model

Think of it like this:

| Concept | Real-world analogy |
|---|---|
| **Git** | A time machine for your code, running on your computer |
| **GitHub** | A cloud backup + sharing site for your time machine |
| **Commit** | A "save point" — a snapshot of your code at a moment in time |
| **Push** | Sending your local save points up to GitHub |
| **Repository (repo)** | The folder being tracked by git (your project) |

The flow is always: **Make changes → Stage them → Commit → Push**

---

## 📍 Step 1 — See What's Changed

Let's look at what files have been modified since the last commit:

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:10:13 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Show current git status]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:10:24 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
---

## 📖 Understanding What You See

Git is telling you:

- **`modified:`** — files that already existed and have been changed
- **`deleted:`** — those `span` junk files that we should get rid of (good riddance!)
- **`Untracked files:`** — brand new files git hasn't seen before

---

## 🧹 Step 2 — Clean Up Junk Files First

Those `._.DS_Store` and `._` files are **macOS system garbage** — they should never be in a repo.
  Let's tell git to permanently ignore them by updating `.gitignore`:

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:10:25 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Read — /home/charles/Documents/prompt-improver/.gitignore]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:10:28 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Edit — /home/charles/Documents/prompt-improver/.gitignore]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:14:56 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
---

## 📦 Step 3 — Stage Your Changes ("git add")

**Staging** means: *"I want these changes included in my next save point."*

Think of it like putting items into a box before sealing it. The commit is sealing the box.

Run this to stage **everything** (all the real changes):

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:14:57 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Stage all changes for commit]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:15:37 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Check what's now staged]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:15:44 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
The junk `._` files are gone (ignored now) and all the real changes are in the green **"Changes to
  be committed"** box. ✅

---

## 💾 Step 4 — Commit ("git commit")

A commit needs a **message** — a short description of what changed. Think of it like a diary entry
  for your code. Good messages say *what* and *why*, not just *"updated stuff"*.

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:15:47 UTC]

[Tool: Bash — Commit all staged changes]

Committed! ✅ Now let's send it to GitHub.

## ☁️ Step 5 — Push to GitHub ("git push")

**Push** uploads your local commits to GitHub so they're safe in the cloud and others (or you, on
  another machine) can see them.

We hit a small authentication hurdle — GitHub needs to verify it's really you before accepting the
  upload. This is normal! Let me explain the fix.

---

## 🔐 The Authentication Problem

GitHub no longer accepts plain passwords. You need to set up one of these:

| Method | Best for |
|---|---|
| **GitHub CLI (`gh`)** | Easiest — guided login in your browser |
| **SSH key** | More technical but very reliable long-term |
| **Personal Access Token** | Middle ground |

For a beginner, **GitHub CLI is the easiest**. Let's install it:

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:17:45 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Check if gh CLI is available to install]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 02:23:21 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
`gh` is available in your package manager. To install and log in, **type this command yourself** in
  the terminal (Claude can't run interactive commands like login):

```bash
! sudo apt install gh -y && gh auth login
```

> 💡 The `!` at the start runs it in this chat session so I can see the output.

**When `gh auth login` runs, it will ask you:**
1. *"What account do you want to log into?"* → **GitHub.com**
2. *"What is your preferred protocol?"* → **HTTPS**
3. *"Authenticate Git with your GitHub credentials?"* → **Yes**
4. *"How would you like to authenticate?"* → **Login with a web browser**
5. It'll give you a code — paste it into the browser window it opens

Once that's done, come back here and I'll push for you! 🚀

---

## 📚 Quick Recap of What You've Learned So Far

```
git status    → see what's changed
git add -A    → stage everything (put it in the box)
git commit -m "message"  → save a snapshot with a label
git push origin main     → upload to GitHub
```

That's the **entire core workflow** — 4 commands, used every day by professional developers.

---

## 📋 Copying from the Terminal

**To copy text:**
> Select it with your mouse → it's automatically copied (no Ctrl+C needed — that stops programs!)

**To paste into the terminal:**
> **Right-click** → Paste
> or
> **Ctrl + Shift + V**

---

## ✨ Even Easier — Just Type It

The command is only 2 words — you can just type it directly:

```
gh auth login
```

> ⚠️ Don't forget the `!` at the very start if you're typing it here in this chat window:
> `! gh auth login`

---

## 🖱️ Or — Click the Copy Button

In the Claude Code interface, code blocks like the one above should have a small **copy icon** in
  the top-right corner when you hover over them. Try hovering over the grey box above and clicking
  that icon, then paste with **Ctrl + Shift + V** in the terminal.

All 7 features are fully implemented and building cleanly! Here's a summary of everything that was
  added:

---

## ✅ What was built

### 1. 🔁 Re-refine from History
Hover over any history item → **"Re-refine"** button appears. Loads the rough prompt back into the
  composer so you can tweak and rerun.

### 2. 📝 Template Variables
Write `{{tone}}` or `{{audience}}` in your prompt → click Refine → a modal pops up asking you to
  fill in each placeholder before sending.

### 3. 📁 Prompt Favourites Folders
In the Saved panel, click **"+ Folder"** to create folders. Hover over any saved prompt → folder
  icon lets you assign it. Folders are collapsible with rename/delete.

### 4. 📊 Analytics Panel
New **Analytics** icon in the left rail. Shows score lift per dimension, overall trend chart (last
  10 refinements), and category breakdown.

### 5. 🔗 Share a Prompt
New **share icon** in the refined prompt header. Generates a local URL (persisted in
  `server/shares.json`) + "Copy as Markdown" for pasting into Slack/email/Notion.

### 6. 🎛️ Custom Scoring Dimensions
In **Settings → Scoring dimensions**: remove built-in ones (Specificity, Audience, etc.) or add your
  own (e.g. "Creativity"). Claude will score your custom dimensions.

### 7. ⛓️ Prompt Chain + Multi-pass
- **Chain panel** (link icon in rail): build a sequential pipeline — step 1's output feeds into
  `{{previous_output}}` in step 2
- **Multi-pass toggle** below the send button: auto-refine 2–5 times for progressively more polished
  results

  1**, then add **drag-and-drop** to Feature 3.

---

## 📝 Feature 2 — Template Variables (Explanation)

Template variables let you build **reusable prompt templates**. Instead of writing a whole new
  prompt each time, you put placeholders like `{{tone}}` or `{{audience}}` in curly braces.

**Example:** Type this in the composer:
```
Write a {{tone}} email to {{recipient}} explaining {{topic}}
```

When you click Refine, a form pops up asking you to fill in the blanks:
- `tone` → *formal*
- `recipient` → *my manager*  
- `topic` → *my holiday request*

It then refines the filled-in version: *"Write a formal email to my manager explaining my holiday
  request"* — so you get a fully refined, specific prompt without typing it all out each time.

You can save these template prompts with placeholders in them and reuse them over and over with
  different values.

Here's a summary of what changed:

## ✅ Feature 1 — Re-refine (Fixed)

The button was invisible because it was positioned on top of the main clickable button (z-index
  issue). It's now completely redesigned:

- Hover over any history item → an **action bar** slides in at the bottom with two buttons:
  - **Load** — restores the full old refinement result
  - **Re-refine** — loads just the rough prompt back into the composer so you can edit and run it
  again fresh

## 📝 Feature 2 — Template Variables (Explained above)

In short: write `{{variable}}` anywhere in your prompt, click Refine, and a form pops up asking for
  the value. Great for reusable prompt structures.

## ✅ Feature 3 — Drag and Drop (Added)

- Every saved prompt card is now **draggable** (cursor changes to a grab hand)
- **Drag it onto any folder** → the folder glows orange to show it's a valid drop target → release
  to move the prompt there
- **Drag onto "Uncategorized"** → removes it from any folder
- The old folder picker dropdown button is gone — dragging is the primary way to organise prompts

The button is definitely in the code ✅. This is a case of the feature being in a **different panel**
  than expected. Here's the distinction:

---

## 🕐 History panel (clock icon)
Shows **every** prompt you've refined — automatic, nothing saved on purpose. No folders here.

## ⭐ Saved prompts panel (star icon)  
Shows only prompts you've deliberately **starred**. This is where the **`+ Folder`** button lives.

---

**To use it:**
1. Click the **⭐ star icon** in the left rail (not the clock)
2. You'll see `Saved` in the header with **`+ Folder`** in the top-right corner
3. You need to have starred at least one prompt first — star a refined prompt using the ★ button in
  the main area

---

That said — **do you also want folders in the History panel?** I can add that too. It would let you
  organise your refinement history into named groups (e.g. "Work prompts", "Personal", "Code"). Just
  say the word and I'll add it.

That's exactly right. Here's what was wrong and what changed:

**Root cause:** With 17 help sections, the `help-nav` list was ~610px tall. Without `flex-shrink: 0`
  or a `max-height`, it would push the content area (`help-body`) completely below the drawer's
  visible bounds on any screen shorter than ~830px. `setActiveSection` *was* running correctly — but
  the content div had 0 visible height, so the user saw nothing change.

**What changed:**

1. **`HelpView` JSX** — wrapped `help-nav` + `help-body` in a new `<div className="help-main">` so
  they form their own flex sub-container inside the drawer

2. **`.help-main` (new CSS)** — `flex: 1; min-height: 0; display: flex; flex-direction: column;
  overflow: hidden` — this takes all remaining drawer height after the logo + head, and distributes
  it between nav and content

3. **`.help-nav` (updated CSS)** — added `flex-shrink: 0` (won't collapse), `max-height: 260px`
  (caps at ~7-8 visible items), `overflow-y: auto` (scrolls for the remaining 9-10 items), and
  `cursor: pointer` on the buttons

4. **`.help-body` (updated CSS)** — added `flex: 1; min-height: 0; overflow-y: auto` so it always
  gets the remaining space and scrolls its content

Refresh the app and try the Help menu — all sections should now be clickable and show their content.

<task>
Replicate the exact design and behavior of claude.ai's left navigation rail in our application.
</task>

<context>
Our current implementation of the left navigation rail differs from claude.ai's in several visible
  ways. The goal is to make ours visually and behaviorally identical to claude.ai's rail.
</context>

<requirements>
Study claude.ai's left navigation rail carefully, then update ours to match it in the following
  respects:

1. **Icon labels**: Every icon in the rail must have a visible text label next to it (e.g., the gear
  icon has the label "Settings"). Match claude.ai's labeling conventions exactly.

2. **Typography**: Use the same font family, font size, font weight, and color as claude.ai's rail
  labels.

3. **Spacing and layout**: Match the icon size, label spacing, vertical padding between items, and
  overall rail width used by claude.ai.

4. **Behavior — collapsed content**: The rail itself must NOT display the contents/children of each
  item inline (as ours currently does). Instead, clicking an icon+label should open that item's
  content in a separate page or dialog box, exactly as claude.ai does. Hovering over an icon when
  the rail is closed should display the label of that icon.

## Comparison: claude.ai left rail vs. ours

---

### 1. Icon labels

**claude.ai:**
The sidebar always displays text labels directly **next to** every icon on the same row, inside an
  expanded rail. Labels like "New chat", "Starred", "Recents" are persistently visible at all times
  — not just on hover. When the sidebar is collapsed to icon-only mode (via a toggle), labels
  disappear and hovering an icon shows a tooltip. The label is rendered in the same row as the icon,
  flush left, using a standard weight (not bold).

**Ours:**
Labels are **never visible** alongside icons. The rail is permanently 52px wide, icon-only. Labels
  only appear as absolutely-positioned dark-pill tooltips that fade in after 250ms on hover
  (`opacity: 0 → 1`). There is no expanded state where labels are alongside icons.

**Change needed:**
Add a proper expanded state to the rail (wider, ~220–260px) where each item renders as an icon+label
  row. The label must be persistently visible, not a tooltip. The existing tooltip mechanism can be
  repurposed for the collapsed-only state.

⚠️ **Uncertainty:** I cannot verify claude.ai's exact label font-size, weight, or colour values
  without live access. The label appears to be ~14px, regular weight (~400), matching the sidebar's
  secondary text colour. **These values need to be confirmed by inspecting claude.ai's CSS in
  DevTools.**

---

### 2. Typography

**claude.ai:**
Labels use what appears to be a **system sans-serif** (or Inter) at approximately **14px**, **font-
  weight 400** (regular — not semibold), colour matching a slightly muted text tone (not full
  primary, not fully secondary). The active/selected item's label appears to shift to a slightly
  brighter or stronger colour.

**Ours:**
Our tooltip labels use `font-size: 12px; font-weight: 500` — smaller and slightly heavier than
  claude.ai's. Our icon buttons have no label typography at all in normal state.

**Change needed:**
When labels are rendered inline (expanded state), use `font-size: 14px; font-weight: 400` and the
  primary text colour variable. The active item label should shift to `font-weight: 500` or the
  accent text colour.

⚠️ **Uncertainty:** The exact colour token (primary vs. slightly muted) cannot be confirmed without
  DevTools. Flag this for manual inspection at `claude.ai` → right-click sidebar label → Inspect →
  Computed Styles.

---

### 3. Spacing and layout

**claude.ai:**
- Expanded rail width: approximately **220–260px** (⚠️ *uncertain — measure with DevTools*)
- Each nav item row: icon (~18–20px) + ~10–12px gap + label text, full-width clickable row
- Vertical padding per item row: approximately **8–10px** top/bottom
- Icon size: approximately **18px** (appears to match ours)
- Top area: logo or avatar section, then a "New chat" primary button, then nav items
- Bottom: user profile section pinned to the bottom

**Ours:**
- Rail width: **52px** fixed, never changes
- Items: 36×36px square buttons, centred, with 4px gaps
- No label column — the horizontal space for labels doesn't exist
- No profile/avatar section at the bottom

**Change needed:**
- Add an expanded/collapsed toggle to the rail
- Expanded width: ~240px (⚠️ *measure against claude.ai to confirm*)
- Each item becomes a full-width flex row: `padding: 8px 12px; gap: 10px; border-radius: 8px`
- Keep the collapsed state at 52px for icon-only display
- The sidebar toggle button controls this switch

---

### 4. Behaviour — content display

**claude.ai:**
Clicking a nav item **does not slide out a sub-panel**. Instead, the main content area to the right
  of the sidebar changes — it becomes a full-width view for that item (e.g., clicking "Starred"
  replaces the chat area with a starred-prompts list). The sidebar itself remains unchanged; it
  doesn't expand or collapse in response to item clicks. The sidebar is a persistent navigation
  rail, not a panel launcher.

**Ours:**
Clicking any item in the rail **slides open a 300px drawer** that overlays the left portion of the
  main content area. The rail itself stays at 52px. Content (history list, settings form, etc.)
  renders inside that drawer panel. Closing the drawer collapses it back.

**Change needed:**
This is the most architecturally significant change. Two possible approaches:

- **Option A (closer to claude.ai):** Make the sidebar fixed-width and have item clicks swap the
  main content area (right of the rail) between the "chat/refinery" view and the panel views
  (history, settings, etc.). The sidebar stays visible at all times; clicking "History" replaces the
  main area with the history panel.
- **Option B (lighter change):** Keep the drawer approach but make the expanded sidebar the drawer
  itself — i.e., widen the rail to ~240px (showing labels), and clicking items shows content in that
  same wider column (making the rail effectively the drawer). This is visually closer without a full
  architecture rewrite.

⚠️ **Architectural risk:** Option A requires rethinking the shell layout significantly. Option B is
  achievable by combining the rail + drawer into one wider fixed panel. **Recommend confirming the
  desired approach before implementing either.**

---

### 5. Visual styling

**claude.ai:**
- **Background:** Slightly darker than the main content area. In dark mode, a dark sidebar tone
  (appears close to `#1a1a1a` or similar) — distinct from but coordinated with the canvas.
- **Active item:** A subtle lighter background fill (appears to be a translucent white/grey
  highlight), **no accent colour** — not the orange/brand colour.
- **Hover state:** Very subtle background tint, slightly lighter than the sidebar background.
- **Icon style:** Outline/stroke icons (matching our current icons). No filled icons.
- **Dividers:** Light separator lines between groups (⚠️ *uncertain whether these exist or not in
  current claude.ai — needs visual confirmation*).
- **No badge/tooltip in expanded state:** Tooltips only show in collapsed (icon-only) mode.

**Ours:**
- **Active item:** Uses `var(--accent-bg)` + `var(--accent-text)` — a warm orange tint. Very visible
  brand colour.
- **Hover:** Uses `var(--bg-surface)` — a slight fill.
- **Rail background:** `var(--bg-rail)` — a dedicated variable but close to the surface colour.
- **Tooltips:** Dark pill (inverted — dark background, light text), used in all states.
- **Icons:** Already outline/stroke style ✓

**Change needed:**
- Active item: Remove the orange accent highlight; switch to a **neutral light-fill** active state
  (e.g., `rgba(255,255,255,0.08)` in dark mode, or a muted grey in light mode)
- Hover: Keep the subtle fill, verify it doesn't use the brand colour
- Tooltips: Only show in collapsed mode; not needed in expanded state

⚠️ **Uncertainty:** The exact active-state background value for claude.ai cannot be confirmed
  without DevTools. The key perceptual difference is *neutral grey* vs. our current *brand orange*.

---

### 6. Recent chats / refined prompts in the rail

**claude.ai:**
Below the navigation icons and labels, claude.ai shows a **scrollable list of recent conversations**
  directly in the sidebar. Each entry shows the conversation title (truncated). Clicking opens that
  conversation in the main area. There may be section headings like "Today", "Yesterday", "Previous
  7 days". The list fills all available vertical space between the nav items and the bottom profile
  section.

**Ours:**
Recent history is **not visible in the rail at all**. It lives inside the History drawer panel,
  which only appears when the History icon is clicked. The rail itself shows nothing except icon
  buttons.

**Change needed:**
Below the nav items in the expanded rail, render a scrollable list of the 10–15 most recent
  refinements. Each entry shows:
- The rough prompt text (truncated to ~40 chars)
- Optionally: the category or timestamp as secondary text
- Click → loads that entry (same as `loadFromHistory()`)

This list needs `flex: 1; overflow-y: auto; min-height: 0` to fill available space without pushing
  the bottom profile section off-screen.

⚠️ **Uncertainty:** Whether claude.ai groups by date ("Today", "Yesterday") or just shows a flat
  list is visible from the app but I cannot confirm the exact grouping headings or font sizes
  without inspecting it.

---

## Prioritised action list

| Priority | Change | Complexity |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Widen the rail to ~240px with persistent icon+label rows** | Medium — CSS + JSX layout
  change |
| 2 | **Show recent refinements in the rail below nav items** | Medium — render from `history[]`
  state |
| 3 | **Replace orange active state with neutral fill** | Small — CSS variable swap |
| 4 | **Collapse/expand toggle** — collapsed = icon-only + tooltip, expanded = icon+label | Medium —
  add `railExpanded` state |
| 5 | **Rethink content display** (drawer vs. full-area swap) | Large — architectural; confirm
  approach before starting |
| 6 | **Date-grouped headings in the recent list** ("Today", "Yesterday") | Small — once the list is
  rendered |

**Before implementing #5:** Confirm whether you want Option A (content replaces main area) or Option
  B (wider rail doubles as the panel). This decision shapes almost everything else. Option B is ~2
  hours of work; Option A is a full layout restructure.

**Values that need live inspection at claude.ai before coding:**
- Expanded rail width (DevTools → `.sidebar` or equivalent → computed width)
- Label font-size and weight (computed styles on a nav label)
- Active-item background-color (computed styles on an active nav item)
- Whether date-grouped headings appear in the chat list

What changed and why each size was chosen:

| Element | Before | After | Why |
|---|---|---|---|
| Body base | 14px | 15px | Cascades to any inherited text (empty state, composer, etc.) |
| Refined prompt | 15px | 16.5px | Main focus of the app — deserves the most generous size |
| Rough prompt | 14px | 15px | Matches the new base |
| Changes title | 13.5px | 14.5px | Stays proportionally smaller than the prompt but more readable |
| Changes explanation | 12.5px | 13.5px | Was the smallest body text in the main area |
| Thinking indicator | 14px | 15px | Matches the new base |

Sidebar labels, panel chrome (drawer-head, etc.), scores, and all the small metadata tags were left
  alone — they're UI fixtures, not reading content.

Done. Run `! git push origin main` to push.

Here's how it works:

- **Expand button** (the outward-arrows icon) appears in the panel header between the + and ×
  buttons. Click it to go fullscreen.
- **Fullscreen state**: the panel expands to cover the entire browser window (`left: 0; width:
  100vw`). The dim backdrop disappears (no accidental close). The main app behind it is unchanged —
  just hidden.
- **Exit fullscreen**: click the compress icon (inward arrows) in the same spot, **or press
  Escape**. The panel animates back to its 520px side-panel state with the backdrop restored.
- **Closing**: the × button closes the panel entirely from either state, returning you to exactly
  where you were.

YOU  [2026-05-26 05:53:12 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
currently when the right pane opens covers it cover the content area what do you propose we do to
  solve this?

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 05:53:55 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
Good question. There are three realistic approaches:

---

## Option A — Dock the panel (push content left) ✅ Recommended

The conversation panel becomes a **flex sibling** of `<main>` inside the shell, exactly like the
  sidebar on the left. When it opens, the main content area shrinks to fill the remaining space. No
  overlay, no backdrop — both areas are always fully visible side by side.

```
[ sidebar 52px ] [ main content — shrinks ] [ conversation panel 520px ]
```

**Pros:** Content always visible while you chat. Professional — the same pattern as VS Code, Linear,
  Notion. Pairs naturally with the fullscreen button (which would still work as a full-cover
  overlay). No backdrop needed.
**Cons:** On small screens the content area gets narrow. Requires moving the RunDrawer from a fixed
  overlay into the shell flex row.

---

## Option B — Replace the content area

When the panel opens, it **replaces** the main content entirely — the same way the left-nav panels
  (History, Settings, etc.) already work. The content disappears while you chat; closing the panel
  brings it back.

```
[ sidebar ] [ conversation panel fills entire main area ]
```

**Pros:** Panel gets maximum space. Architecturally very simple (one line of change).  
**Cons:** You lose sight of the refined prompt you were chatting about. Breaks the "run this prompt
  and see results" workflow.

---

## Option C — Narrow overlay that doesn't fully cover

Keep the fixed overlay but reduce the panel width to ~380px and constrain the backdrop to only the
  right portion. Content on the left is still partially readable.

**Pros:** Minimal code change.  
**Cons:** Still an overlay. Content is squeezed but not properly reachable. Feels like a compromise,
  not a solution.

---

## Recommendation

**Option A.** It's the correct architectural answer and it's what the sidebar redesign already set
  up as a pattern. The shell is already a flex row — adding the conversation panel as a third flex
  child is a natural extension of what's already there.

Which would you like me to implement?

CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 07:59:13 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
The layout is fine — the sidebar **does not** cover the content area. Here's why:

**`.shell`** is `display: flex` (a flex row). Its three children are:

| Element | CSS | Behaviour |
|---|---|---|
| `.sidebar` | `flex-shrink: 0; width: 52px / 240px` | Takes exactly its declared width, never
  shrinks |
| `.main` | `flex: 1; min-width: 0` | Fills **all remaining space** — shrinks when sidebar expands
  or panel opens |
| `.run-drawer` | `flex-shrink: 0; width: 520px` | Takes its declared width when open |

No `position: fixed` or `position: absolute` on any of those three — they're all normal flex
  children sitting side by side. When the sidebar expands from 52 → 240px, the `main` smoothly
  absorbs the difference because `flex: 1` redistributes space automatically.

The only thing that ever overlays the content is `.run-drawer--fullscreen` (when you hit the expand
  button), which deliberately uses `position: fixed; inset: 0` to cover everything. That's
  intentional.

So the left panel is already working correctly — it **pushes** rather than **covers**.

Done. Here's what changed:

- **No more "Recent" heading** — the section just flows directly below the nav items, separated by a
  subtle `border-top` divider
- **Flex rows** — each history item is a `.sidebar-recent-row` that handles the hover background, so
  the text and delete button share one highlight target
- **Hidden × delete button** — `.sidebar-recent-delete` sits at `opacity: 0` until the row is
  hovered, then fades in; clicking it calls the new `deleteHistoryEntry()` and removes just that
  entry without touching the rest of history
- **`deleteHistoryEntry(timestamp)`** — filters the history array, updates both state and
  `localStorage`, and removes the key entirely if history becomes empty

Done. Here's what was added:

**Expanded sidebar** — a full-width bordered button sits between the logo row and the nav items,
  with `+` on the left and "New rough prompt" as the label. Hovering fills it with the subtle
  background exactly like the nav items.

**Collapsed sidebar** — the label disappears and the border is dropped, leaving just the `+` icon
  centred — matching the icon-only style of the other collapsed items.

**Clicking it**:
1. Closes any open panel (History, Settings, etc.)
2. Closes the conversation drawer if open
3. Clears the rough prompt, submitted prompt, feedback, and any error
4. Clears the refined output, scores, changes, and comparison
5. Focuses the composer textarea

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - React 19 SPA, single `App.jsx` monolith (~5500+ lines after recent additions)
   - Express 5 backend with SSE streaming on port 3001
   - CSS flexbox shell layout: sidebar | main | run-drawer as flex siblings
   - localStorage persistence for all client state
   - SSE streaming via `consumeSSE` → typed wrappers (`streamRefinement` etc.)
   - `useRef` pattern for abort controllers and pending state (e.g., `pendingPassTotalRef`)
   - Native `fetch` in Node 18+ for Notion/Slack API calls (no extra npm deps needed)
   - Notion API: `POST https://api.notion.com/v1/pages` with `Authorization: Bearer {token}` and
  `Notion-Version: 2022-06-28`
   - Slack webhooks: `POST {webhookUrl}` with JSON `{ text: "..." }`
   - Version tracking pattern: closure captures `passNum`/`passTotal` in `onDone` callback; versions
  stored as `[{id, label, improved, changes, scores, model, feedback, ts}]`

       ```javascript
       useEffect(() => {
         function onKey(e) {
           if (e.key === 'Escape' && !confirmState && !piiFindings && !templateVarsOpen &&
  !shareModalOpen && !pdfModalOpen && !importExportOpen) {
             if (activeView !== null) { e.preventDefault(); setActiveView(null); }
           }
           if (e.key === '/' && document.activeElement?.tagName !== 'INPUT' &&
  document.activeElement?.tagName !== 'TEXTAREA') {
             e.preventDefault();
             setActiveView(null);
             setTimeout(() => textareaRef.current?.focus(), 60);
           }
         }
         window.addEventListener('keydown', onKey);
         return () => window.removeEventListener('keydown', onKey);
       }, [activeView, confirmState, piiFindings, templateVarsOpen, shareModalOpen, pdfModalOpen,
  importExportOpen]);
       ```

   - **`server/index.js`**
     - **`POST /api/export/notion`** route (added before `app.listen`):
       - Accepts: `{ rough, improved, changes, category, model, token, databaseId }`
       - Calls `https://api.notion.com/v1/pages` with `Authorization: Bearer {token}`, `Notion-
  Version: 2022-06-28`
       - Creates page with title, Original/Refined headings and paragraph blocks, What Changed
  section
       - Returns `{ ok: true, url, id }` on success, error JSON on failure
     - **`POST /api/export/slack`** route:
       - Accepts: `{ rough, improved, changes, category, model, webhookUrl }`
       - POSTs formatted Slack message with blockquoted original/refined + bullet-point changes
       - Returns `{ ok: true }` or error JSON

   - **`client/src/help-content.js`**
     - Fixed folders section: changed "drop it onto a folder header" to accurate description of
  dragging onto the folder section body; added mention of dragging back to Uncategorized

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **Multi-pass bypasses template-variable and PII checks**: `handleImprove()` was calling
  `executeRefinement()` directly when multi-pass was enabled, skipping the `runRefinement()` which
  contains the template-var and PII scanner guards. Fixed by introducing `pendingPassTotalRef` and
  routing all calls through `runRefinement()`.
   - **Help docs inaccuracy — folders "header"**: The Folders help section said "drag onto a folder
  header" but the actual drop target in `FolderSection` is the whole section div, not just the
  header row. Fixed to say "drag onto a folder".
   - **confirm() dialogs are native browser blocking alerts**: All 7 replaced with the custom non-
  blocking `ConfirmDialog` component using `showConfirm()` pattern.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Multi-pass + template vars/PII**: Solved by storing pass count in a ref
  (`pendingPassTotalRef`) set at the top of `handleImprove`, then reading it in `runRefinement` and
  `handlePIIContinue` so the pass count survives the modal interruptions.
   - **Version display without losing live state**: Solved via computed variables
  (`displayImproved`, `displayChanges`, `displayScores`) — when viewing an older version, these
  shadow the live state; "Use this version" promotes the version back into live state.
   - **Claude.ai sidebar design**: Matched by adding `sidebar-recent-row` flex container with
  opacity-0 delete button that becomes opacity-1 on hover, removing the "Recent" heading, and adding
  a border-top divider.

All done. Here's a summary of everything completed this session:

---

## What was built

### Export to Notion & Slack
- **Server**: `POST /api/export/notion` creates a structured page in a Notion database; `POST
  /api/export/slack` posts a formatted message via Incoming Webhook
- **Settings → Integrations**: New section with fields for Notion token, database ID, and Slack
  webhook URL — all stored locally in the browser
- **Export dropdown** (⤴ button) in the refined prompt action bar opens a Notion/Slack picker
- Error toasts if credentials aren't configured

### Prompt Diff Viewer
- **Diff button** in the refined prompt action bar toggles a word-level diff panel
- Pure LCS algorithm (`computeWordDiff`) in `utils.js` — no external deps
- Deleted tokens shown in red strikethrough, inserted tokens in green
- Stat badges show counts of removed/added word groups
- Diff auto-closes when a new refinement starts

### App.jsx Split (61% size reduction)
**Before:** 5,473 lines | **After:** 2,136 lines

New modules extracted:

| File | Contents |
|---|---|
| `constants.js` | MODELS, PRICING, STORAGE_*, DEFAULT_SETTINGS, QUICK_STARTS |
| `utils.js` | Pure utilities: formatTime, computeCost, computeWordDiff, etc. |
| `sse.js` | consumeSSE, streamRefinement, streamComparison, etc. |
| `PDFPreviewModal.jsx` | 570-line PDF modal |
| `LeftRailViews.jsx` | All 10 left-rail panels + ImportExportModal |
| `ScoreComponents.jsx` | Skeletons, RadarChart, ScoresPanel, ChangesPanel |
| `ComparisonPanels.jsx` | CompareInvite, ComparisonColumn, ComparisonStrip |
| `ABTestPanels.jsx` | ABTestPanel, ABTestInvite, FollowUpPanel |
| `Modals.jsx` | PIIWarning, TemplateVars, Share, PromptDiff, ConfirmDialog, ToastList |

## Prompt Refinery — Test Plan

### Setup
```bash
# Terminal 1
cd server && npm run dev     # → http://localhost:3001

# Terminal 2
cd client && npm run dev     # → http://localhost:5173
```

---

### 1 — Template Variables

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Type `Write a {{tone}} email to {{audience}}` in the composer | |
| 2 | Click **Refine** | Modal "Fill in variables" appears with 2 labelled inputs |
| 3 | Leave one blank and click **Continue** | Button stays disabled |
| 4 | Fill both fields and click **Continue** | Modal closes, refinement starts with variables
  substituted |
| 5 | Type a prompt with NO `{{...}}` and refine | Modal does NOT appear |

---

### 2 — Re-refine from History

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Refine at least one prompt so History has an entry | |
| 2 | Open **History** in left rail | |
| 3 | Click **Re-refine** on an entry | Composer loads with that rough prompt; feedback input is
  focused |
| 4 | Modify the feedback text and click Refine | New refinement runs as a follow-up |

---

### 3 — Prompt Favourites Folders

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Refine a prompt and click the ★ icon | Prompt saved |
| 2 | Open **Saved prompts** → click **+ Folder** | Name input appears |
| 3 | Type a folder name and press Enter | Folder created with item count 0 |
| 4 | Drag a saved prompt onto the folder | Prompt moves into the folder |
| 5 | Drag the prompt back to **Uncategorized** | Prompt returns to uncategorized |
| 6 | Click the pencil icon on the folder | Inline rename works |
| 7 | Delete the folder | Folder removed; prompt moves back to Uncategorized |

---

### 4 — History Analytics

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Ensure at least 3 refinements in History | |
| 2 | Open **Analytics** in left rail | Summary cards show refinement count, avg refined score, avg
  lift |
| 3 | Check "Score lift by dimension" bars | Bars render with + / − values |
| 4 | Check "By category" bars | Categories proportional to actual history |
| 5 | With < 2 scored entries | Empty state message shown |

---

### 5 — Share a Prompt

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Refine a prompt | |
| 2 | Click the **Share** icon (🔗) in action bar | Share modal opens with a localhost URL |
| 3 | Click **Copy link** | "Copied!" feedback, URL in clipboard |
| 4 | Open URL in a new tab | Static page shows Original / Refined / Changes |
| 5 | Click **Copy as Markdown** | Clipboard contains formatted Markdown with headings |

---

### 6 — Custom Scoring Dimensions

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Open **Settings** → scroll to **Scoring dimensions** | 5 default chips visible |
| 2 | Click × on "Format" chip | Chip turns grey/crossed |
| 3 | Click **+ Add dimension** → enter "Creativity" + description → **Add** | New chip appears |
| 4 | Refine a prompt | Scorecard shows Creativity dimension; Format dimension absent |
| 5 | Click **Reset to defaults** | All chips restored; custom ones removed |

---

### 7A — Prompt Chain

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Open **Prompt Chain** in left rail | Empty state with "+ Add first step" |
| 2 | Click + Step twice | 2 step cards appear |
| 3 | In Step 1 enter `Summarise this in 3 bullet points: The sky is blue.` | |
| 4 | In Step 2 enter `Now translate the following to French: {{previous_output}}` | |
| 5 | Click **Run chain** | Step 1 runs; its output injected into Step 2; Step 2 runs with
  translated result |
| 6 | Click **Copy** on Step 2 output | Clipboard has French text |
| 7 | Reorder steps with ↑/↓ buttons | Steps swap correctly |
| 8 | Delete a step | Step removed |

---

### 7B — Multi-pass Refinement

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Enable the **Multi-pass** toggle below the composer | Pass count selector (2–5) appears |
| 2 | Set to 3 passes | |
| 3 | Enter a rough prompt and click Refine | Progress indicator "Pass 2 of 3…" then "Pass 3 of 3…"
  visible |
| 4 | Refinement completes | Final output is the 3rd-pass refined prompt |
| 5 | Disable Multi-pass and refine again | Single pass, no progress indicator |

---

### 8 — Prompt Versioning

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Refine a prompt, then send follow-up feedback twice | `v3` badge appears in action bar |
| 2 | Click the version badge | Versions panel expands showing v1, v2, v3 |
| 3 | Click v1 in the panel | Older refined text, changes, and scores display |
| 4 | Click **Use this version** | Live state promoted to v1's content |

---

### 9 — Export to Notion / Slack

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Open **Settings → Integrations** | Fields for Notion token, database ID, Slack webhook |
| 2 | Click ⤴ export button without credentials configured | Toast: "Add your Notion token…" error |
| 3 | Enter a valid Notion token + database ID | |
| 4 | Refine a prompt → click ⤴ → **Export to Notion** | Toast: "Exported to Notion ✓" |
| 5 | Enter a valid Slack webhook URL | |
| 6 | Click ⤴ → **Post to Slack** | Toast: "Posted to Slack ✓" |

---

### 10 — Prompt Diff Viewer

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Refine a prompt | |
| 2 | Click **Diff** button in action bar | Word-level diff panel appears below the refined prompt |
| 3 | Check deleted text | Shown in red with strikethrough |
| 4 | Check inserted text | Shown in green |
| 5 | Stat badges show −N removed, +M added | Counts are non-zero |
| 6 | Click **Diff** again | Panel hides |
| 7 | Start a new refinement | Diff auto-closes |

---

### 11 — Polish / UX

| Step | Action | Expected |
|---|---|---|
| Press `Esc` with left rail open | Rail closes | |
| Press `/` from any non-input context | Composer textarea focuses | |
| Click any destructive action (Clear history, delete folder, etc.) | Custom confirm dialog appears
  (no native browser `confirm()`) | |
| Import a `.json` export file | Toast shows imported count | |
| Export to PDF → toggle sections | PDF regenerates with only selected sections | |

────────────────────────────────────────
YOU  [2026-05-26 10:08:28 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
do you think is possible to have a feature that allows the use to edit refined prompts? (tweaking
  it)

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:08:57 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
Yes, very doable — and it's a natural gap in the current flow. Right now the refined prompt is read-
  only, so if Claude gets 90% right but you want to tweak a sentence, you'd have to copy it
  somewhere else. Here's what I'd build:

---

### How it would work

A **pencil/edit button** in the action bar (alongside Save, Share, etc.). Clicking it puts the
  refined prompt into an editable textarea. While editing:

- The action bar swaps to **"Save edits"** + **"Cancel"**
- `Ctrl+Enter` / `⌘+Enter` saves
- `Escape` cancels

On **Save**:
- The edited text replaces the live `improvedPrompt` state
- A new version entry is pushed to the version history, labelled **"v2 (edited)"** — so you can
  always diff the AI's original output against your tweak
- The diff viewer, PDF export, copy button, star/save, and follow-up refinement all use your edited
  version going forward

---

### What stays the same

- You can still send a follow-up refinement on top of your manual edit (it uses the edited text as
  the "previous refined" base)
- The diff viewer will show your edit vs the original rough prompt — useful to see the full delta
- Saving to favourites preserves your edited version, not Claude's raw output

---

### One design question

**Should manual edits feed back into the "Re-refine" flow?** That is — if you open a history entry
  that you had manually edited, should "Re-refine" start from your edited version or Claude's
  original? I'd lean toward your edited version since that's what you actually used.

---

Want me to build it? It's roughly:

1. `editingRefined` + `editDraft` state
2. PencilIcon toggle in action bar → textarea swap

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- React 19 SPA, Express 5 backend, SSE streaming on port 3001
- Modular component extraction (constants.js, utils.js, sse.js, PDFPreviewModal.jsx,
  LeftRailViews.jsx, ScoreComponents.jsx, ComparisonPanels.jsx, ABTestPanels.jsx, Modals.jsx)
- LCS (Longest Common Subsequence) algorithm for word-level diff computation — pure JS, no external
  deps
- Prompt versioning: `promptVersions` array stores `{id, label, improved, changes, scores, model,
  feedback, ts}` entries; computed display vars (`displayImproved`, `displayChanges`,
  `displayScores`) shadow live state when viewing older versions
- `useRef` pattern for abort controllers and DOM refs (editTextareaRef for the new edit textarea)
- localStorage persistence with writer functions that update both React state and localStorage in
  one call
- Notion API: `POST https://api.notion.com/v1/pages` with `Authorization: Bearer {token}` and
  `Notion-Version: 2022-06-28`
- Slack webhooks: `POST {webhookUrl}` with JSON `{ text: "..." }`
- Python script used to do the large App.jsx replacement (replacing lines 1–3397 atomically)
- Vite build used for verification after each change

4. Errors and Fixes:

- No build errors were encountered during this session — all `npm run build` calls succeeded cleanly

  1–3397 rather than using the Edit tool (which has exact-match requirements that would be fragile
  over such a large section)

---

5. Problem Solving:

- **App.jsx split strategy**: Instead of making many fragile Edit calls on a 5,473-line file, used a
  Python script to replace everything before `function App()` atomically, then kept App() body
  unchanged. This was the safest approach.
- **LEFT_RAIL_ITEMS placement**: Kept in App.jsx (not constants.js) because it references JSX icon
  components and a .js file can't import JSX without being a .jsx file.
- **DEFAULT_CHAIN_STEP**: Moved to LeftRailViews.jsx since it's only used inside ChainView. App()
  just passes callbacks, never calls DEFAULT_CHAIN_STEP directly.
- **computeWordDiff duplication**: Initially defined in App.jsx inline; moved to utils.js for the
  split so Modals.jsx (PromptDiffPanel) can import it cleanly.
- **SmallRadarChart in ComparisonPanels.jsx**: ComparisonColumn uses a small radar chart. Rather
  than importing from ScoreComponents.jsx (which would create a cross-dependency concern), a local
  simplified SmallRadarChart was defined inline in ComparisonPanels.jsx.

CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:33:09 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
Everything is wired up correctly. Here's a summary of what was added for the **inline edit**
  feature:

---

### Inline Edit of Refined Prompts ✅

**How it works:**

1. **Edit button** — A pencil icon button appears in the refined prompt's action bar (between Diff
  and Copy). It's enabled only when refinement is complete and nothing is streaming.

2. **Edit mode** — Clicking the pencil replaces:
   - The read-only `message-body` div → a full-width `<textarea>` pre-filled with the current
  refined text, with an accent-coloured border so it's visually distinct from view mode
   - All action buttons → just **Save edits** (accent-coloured) and **Cancel**

3. **Keyboard shortcuts** — `⌘↵` / `Ctrl+↵` saves; `Escape` cancels, no changes made.

4. **Versioning** — Saving pushes a new entry to `promptVersions` labelled `"v3 (edited)"` (or
  whatever the next version number is), so the edit appears in the version history panel and is
  fully undoable by browsing back.

5. **Toast** — A success toast confirms `"Edit saved as v2 (edited)"`.

6. **Auto-reset** — `clearCurrentRefinement()` exits edit mode, so starting a fresh refinement never
  leaves a dangling edit state.

Done. When the sidebar is expanded you'll now see:

- **Nav items** (History, Saved, etc.)
- **Starred** — filled star icon header, then up to 5 saved prompts as clickable rows. If a saved
  prompt has been given a name it shows that; otherwise it shows the truncated rough prompt text.
  The currently-loaded saved prompt is highlighted in accent colour. If there are more than 5, a `+N
  more` link at the bottom jumps straight to the full Saved panel.

CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:43:01 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
Found it. `FunnelLogo` is missing from the import — it's used inside `{railExpanded && ...}` which
  is why the app works when collapsed (short-circuit skips it) but crashes the moment you expand
  (JavaScript evaluates the reference and throws `ReferenceError: FunnelLogo is not defined`).

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:43:03 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Edit — /home/charles/Documents/prompt-improver/client/src/App.jsx]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:43:08 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Verify build passes]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:43:17 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
[Tool: Bash — Commit the import fix]

────────────────────────────────────────
CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:43:26 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
That was the culprit. `FunnelLogo` was referenced inside `{railExpanded && ...}` — JavaScript's `&&`
  short-circuit meant the reference was never evaluated while the sidebar stayed collapsed, so the
  app ran fine. The moment you expanded it, the expression was reached and threw `ReferenceError:
  FunnelLogo is not defined`, which React caught and replaced the whole tree with a blank page.

This was a pre-existing bug from the refactor (the import got dropped during the module split). The
  starred section I added yesterday didn't introduce it, but did cause you to expand the sidebar for
  the first time and hit it. Fixed now — `FunnelLogo` is properly imported.

CLAUDE  [2026-05-26 10:49:15 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
The original 7-feature plan is fully shipped. Here's what I think would give the most bang for the
  next round:

---

### Quick wins (1 session each)

**🔍 Search / filter in History & Saved**
As those lists grow, scrolling gets tedious. A small search box at the top of each panel that
  filters by rough prompt text, category, or model. No backend needed.

**🔢 Token counter in the composer**
Show a live estimated token count below the textarea (word count × ~1.3 is a decent approximation).
  Helps users feel confident before hitting Refine.

**⌨️ Keyboard shortcut cheatsheet**
A `?` button (or `Shift+?`) that pops a small modal listing all shortcuts (⌘↵, /, Esc, etc.). Pure
  discoverability — no new logic.

---

### Medium lift

**🌙 Dark mode**
The app is warm-beige only right now. A toggle in Settings that swaps the CSS variables to a dark
  palette. All the components already use CSS vars so the blast radius is just `:root[data-
  theme="dark"]` overrides.

**📌 Pin to top in History**
Let users pin important refinements so they stay at the top of the history list regardless of date.
  Stored as a `pinned: true` flag on the history entry.

---

### Bigger

**🔔 Prompt improvement tips / AI critique mode**
After refining, add an optional "Critique this refined prompt" button that calls the API a second
  time and asks Claude to identify any remaining weaknesses. Returns bullet points rather than a
  full refinement.

---

What sounds most useful to you? Or if you have something else in mind entirely, let's do that.

You're already on **Claude Sonnet 4.6** (the model powering this session). To switch to the most
  capable model available:

**In Claude Code CLI**, run:

```bash
claude --model claude-opus-4-7
```

Or set it permanently in your Claude Code settings with `/model` — type:

```
/model claude-opus-4-7
```

**`claude-opus-4-7`** is the current top-tier model — most capable, best for complex coding tasks.
  That's the one you want for top-class work.

The trade-off is it's a bit slower and costs more per token, but for the kind of feature work we've
  been doing together, it's worth it.

Sleep well, Charles! 🌙

Welcome back! Great that you're refreshed. 

Here's where the project stands and what I'd suggest tackling next:

---

### 🔧 Quick wins worth doing first

**Switch the app's default model to Opus 4.7**
You just set Claude Code to Opus 4.7 — but Prompt Refinery itself still defaults to Sonnet 4.6. A
  one-line change in `constants.js`.

**Dark mode polish pass**
Dark mode was added but not exhaustively tested. Some components (modals, dropdowns, the run drawer,
  code blocks) likely have hard-coded colours that don't respect the theme. Worth a sweep.

---

### 🚀 Meaningful next features

**Prompt history search in the sidebar**
Right now the sidebar Recents list is just a static scroll. Adding inline search there (not just
  inside the History panel) would match how Claude.ai works.

**Conversation summary / auto-title**
The Run Drawer conversations auto-title from the first message, but there's no way to see a summary
  of what was discussed. A one-click "Summarise this conversation" button would be handy.

**Prompt quality score over time chart**
The Analytics panel has stats but no time-series line chart showing how your average score is
  improving session over session.

**Export to CSV from the Usage panel**
The Usage panel shows cost data but you can't export it. Useful for tracking spend.

---

### What do you want to do?

I'd recommend starting with **the default model switch + a dark mode polish pass** since they're
  fast and affect every session going forward. Then pick whichever feature appeals most.

What sounds good to you?

CLAUDE  [2026-05-27 02:54:45 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
Great! Here's an honest look at where the app stands and what would move the needle most from here:

---

### 🎯 Highest impact next moves

**Custom refinement instructions**
A text field in Settings — "Always refine for X style" or "I'm a senior backend engineer, keep
  prompts technical." This persona/instruction gets passed with every `/api/improve` call so Claude
  refines with your context in mind. High value, small effort.

**Batch refinement**
A "Batch" panel where you paste multiple rough prompts (one per line or as a list), hit Run, and
  they all get refined in parallel. Results shown in a grid you can copy or save individually.

**Mobile layout**
The app works on desktop but is basically unusable on a phone. A responsive layout pass would make
  it usable from anywhere.

---

### ⚙️ Technical health

**Code splitting**
The JS bundle is 1.77MB — it all loads upfront. Splitting by route (lazy-load the heavy panels)
  would cut initial load time significantly.

**Prompt history deduplication at save time**
Right now duplicate rough prompts can pile up in history. A quick check before saving would keep
  history clean.

---

### 💡 Nice-to-haves

- **Tag system** on history entries (e.g. `#work`, `#side-project`) for better organisation
- **Prompt complexity score** shown before refining — an instant heuristic gauge of how detailed the
  rough prompt is
- **PWA support** — installable as a desktop app with an icon

---

What order would you like to tackle these? I'd personally start with **custom refinement
  instructions** — it directly improves every single refinement you do and takes about 30 minutes to
  build end-to-end.

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- React 19 SPA (Vite, port 5173)
- Express 5 backend with SSE streaming (port 3001)
- Chrome Manifest V3 extension
- CSS custom properties for theming (`--bg-canvas`, `--accent`, etc.); dark mode via `:root[data-
  theme="dark"]` overrides
- SSE event pattern: `setupSSE()` + `sendEvent(res, eventName, data)`
- Custom delimiter parsing: `<<<REFINED_PROMPT>>>`, `<<<CHANGES_JSON>>>`, `<<<SCORES_JSON>>>`,
  `<<<END>>>`
- `buildSystemPrompt(dimensions)` — dynamic system prompt builder
- `consumeSSE(response, handlers)` — generic SSE reader in sse.js
- `streamRefinement`, `streamComparison`, `streamTest`, `streamRunPrompt`, `streamCritique` — typed
  SSE wrappers
- `promptVersions` array for versioning each refined output
- `AbortController` refs for every streaming operation
- localStorage persistence via typed setter functions
- `&&` short-circuit in JSX can hide undefined component references (FunnelLogo bug lesson)
- SVG-based charts (hand-rolled, no external library): RadarChart, ScoreTrendChart
- `React.lazy()` + `Suspense` considered for code splitting

---

export const DEFAULT_SETTINGS = {

  `streamCritique`

  `critiqueAbortRef`, `sidebarQuery`, `convoSummary`, `summarising`, `summaryAbortRef`
- `darkMode` useEffect: applies/removes `data-theme="dark"` on `document.documentElement`
- `togglePinEntry(timestamp)`: sorts pinned items to top, persists to localStorage
- `handleStartEdit()`, `handleSaveEdit()`, `handleCancelEdit()`: inline edit handlers

  get 3-5 bullet summary

  matches" state

  `critiqueDone`

---

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **FunnelLogo crash on sidebar expand**: App showed blank black page when expanding sidebar.
  `FunnelLogo` was used inside `{railExpanded && ...}` but never imported in App.jsx. JavaScript
  `&&` short-circuit hid the ReferenceError when collapsed; expanding triggered it. Fixed by adding
  `FunnelLogo` to icons import. Lesson: Vite build does NOT catch undefined JSX component references
  — only blow up at runtime when branch is taken.

- **Duplicate fetch in handleSummariseConvo**: Initially wrote code that called `fetch()` once AND
  `streamRunPrompt()` on the same endpoint (double request). Fixed immediately by removing the
  direct `fetch()` call and keeping only `streamRunPrompt()`.

- **User pushed to GitHub manually**: Assistant attempted `git push origin main` but was blocked by
  Claude Code permission system (requires explicit authorization to push to default branch). User
  pushed manually.

---

5. Problem Solving:

- **App.jsx size management**: File was split into 9 modules (constants, utils, sse, icons,
  PDFPreviewModal, LeftRailViews, ScoreComponents, ComparisonPanels, ABTestPanels, Modals) in a
  previous session. New code is added to appropriate module rather than back into App.jsx monolith.

- **Dark mode implementation**: Used CSS custom properties (`var(--*)`) throughout, so `:root[data-
  theme="dark"]` overrides cascade automatically to all components. Only hard-coded colors (like
  `background: white` on PDF iframe, diff token colors) needed component-level overrides.

- **ScoreTrendChart**: Hand-rolled SVG (no external charting library) following same pattern as
  existing RadarChart, keeping bundle size manageable.

- **Conversation summary UX**: Rather than a new API endpoint, reused existing `/api/run-prompt`
  with a transcript built from `currentConvo.messages` and a summary instruction. Summary shown as a
  dismissible banner (not a conversation turn) to keep it separate from the chat.

CLAUDE  [2026-05-27 03:10:05 UTC]
────────────────────────────────────────
All 8 features are done and committed. Here's a summary of everything that was shipped:

---

## ✅ All 8 features implemented

### 1. Custom Refinement Instructions
**Settings → "Custom refinement instructions"** — a textarea where you write style guidance like
  *"Always use bullet points"* or *"Keep prompts under 150 words"*. It's appended to every
  `/api/improve` call on both first-pass and follow-up refinements. Character counter (max 1,000).

### 2. History Deduplication
`saveToHistory` now checks the `rough + improved + model` triple before inserting. Identical re-runs
  are silently skipped — no more bloated history from repeatedly refining the same prompt.

### 3. Prompt Complexity Score
Live **1–5 gauge** (🔴 Vague → 🔵 Complex) next to the token counter in the composer. Updates as you
  type. Scores word count + structural signals (bullets, numbered lists,
  format/constraint/audience/example keywords).

### 4. Tag System on History Entries
Each history entry now has **tag chips** — click `+ tag` to add any label, `×` to remove. A **tag
  filter bar** appears above the list when any tags exist, letting you instantly filter to a
  specific tag. Tags persist in localStorage with the history.

### 5. Batch Refinement Panel
New **Batch Refine** panel in the left rail. Add up to 10 prompts, hit **Run** — they all stream in
  parallel via the existing `/api/improve` endpoint. Each result card shows live streaming output,
  status indicators (⚡ Running / ✓ Done / ✗ Error), copy button, and auto-saves to History.

### 6. Code Splitting
`PDFPreviewModal` and `RunDrawer` are now `React.lazy()` dynamic imports wrapped in `<Suspense>`.
  `autoTitle` moved to `utils.js` to enable true splitting. **Main bundle: 1,172 kB → 380 kB (67%
  reduction)**. The heavy chunks only load when the user actually opens the PDF modal or
  conversation drawer.

### 7. Mobile Layout
Additional `@media (max-width: 640px/480px)` breakpoints; complexity badge hidden on small screens;
  batch controls stack vertically on mobile; drawer heads wrap gracefully; improved touch targets.

### 8. PWA Support
`/public/manifest.json` with name, theme color (`#7c3aed`), and SVG icon. `index.html` now has
  `<link rel="manifest">`, `<meta name="theme-color">`, Apple Web App meta tags, and `viewport-
  fit=cover` for notch devices. The app is now **installable** from Chrome/Edge/Safari as a desktop
  or mobile app.
